# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kafka SASL Mechanism Configuration Validation

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that validate SASL mechanism configuration at broker startup: the sasl.enabled.mechanisms validation, the JAAS config presence check, and the mechanism-specific configuration validation (SCRAM, GSSAPI, OAUTHBEARER).

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the compliance domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

## Summary

I've analyzed the Kafka codebase (github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489) and created a comprehensive report documenting **16 key Java files** that perform SASL mechanism validation. The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json`.

### Key Validation Points Found:

1. **sasl.enabled.mechanisms validation** (KafkaConfig.scala): Ensures the inter-broker SASL mechanism is included in enabled mechanisms

2. **JAAS config presence check**:
   - JaasContext.java: Validates JAAS context entries exist
   - JaasConfig.java: Parses and validates that login modules are specified

3. **Mechanism-specific configuration validation**:
   - **SCRAM**: ScramServerCallbackHandler, ScramSaslServer
   - **GSSAPI**: Handled in SaslChannelBuilder and SaslServerAuthenticator  
   - **OAUTHBEARER**: OAuthBearerValidatorCallbackHandler, BrokerJwtValidator, OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler
   - **PLAIN**: PlainServerCallbackHandler

### Validation Chain:
1. KafkaConfig.validate() - Initial checks
2. ChannelBuilders.serverChannelBuilder() - Creates channel builder
3. SaslChannelBuilder.configure() - Core validation orchestration
4. JaasContext.loadServerContext() - JAAS configuration loading
5. SaslServerAuthenticator - Final validation checks

The answer includes complete details about all files, key validation methods, and a narrative explanation of how the validation chain works at broker startup.

This method is critical and performs multiple validations: (1) it loads JAAS contexts for each enabled mechanism via JaasContext.loadServerContext() which first validates presence of JAAS configuration entries (JaasContext.java lines 145-150) and ensures exactly one login module exists (lines 92-98). JaasContext then calls JaasConfig constructor (JaasConfig.java) which parses the JAAS configuration and validates that at least one login module is specified (line 66). This method is critical and performs multiple validations: (1) it loads JAAS contexts for each enabled mechanism via JaasContext.loadServerContext() which first validates presence of JAAS configuration entries (JaasContext.java lines 145-150) and ensures exactly one login module exists (lines 92-98). (3) it creates LoginManager instances for each mechanism via LoginManager.acquireLoginManager() (lines 170) which loads JAAS login contexts; (4) it configures each callback handler with mechanism parameters (line 151). For OAUTHBEARER specifically, OAuthBearerValidatorCallbackHandler.configure() (lines 106-114) delegates to getConfiguredInstance to instantiate the JwtValidator, and BrokerJwtValidator.configure() (lines 107-139) validates OAUTHBEARER-specific configuration like clock skew, audience, and issuer. Finally, SaslServerAuthenticator constructor (lines 178-189) validates that sasl.enabled.mechanisms is non-empty and that callback handlers and subjects exist for each enabled mechanism. ScramSaslServer performs mechanism validation to ensure SCRAM mechanisms are properly registered.
